# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Architecture Document: Envoy HTTP Connection Manager

**Repository:** envoyproxy/envoy
**Output:** Write your document to `/workspace/documentation.md`

## Task

Produce an architecture document for Envoy's **HTTP Connection Manager** (HCM) subsystem. The document must explain how the major components interact to process an HTTP request from arrival on a downstream connection through to upstream dispatch. Do not simply list APIs — explain the **design**, **data flow**, and **extension points**.

## Scope

Your document must cover these four components and how they work together:

### 1. ConnectionManagerImpl
The central network filter that owns the connection lifecycle. Explain:
- How it implements `Network::ReadFilter` to receive raw bytes
- How it creates and manages `ActiveStream` objects for each HTTP request
- Its role in codec creation (lazy codec instantiation for H1/H2 vs. H3)
- Connection-level concerns: drain decisions, overload management, watermark-based flow control

### 2. FilterManager and the HTTP Filter Chain
The per-stream filter chain execution engine. Explain:
- The decoder filter chain (request path) and encoder filter chain (response path)
- How `FilterChainFactory` creates filters for each stream
- Filter iteration: how `decodeHeaders`/`decodeData`/`decodeTrailers` propagate through decoder filters
- How filters can stop iteration, modify headers, or send local replies
- The distinction between `StreamDecoderFilter`, `StreamEncoderFilter`, and `StreamFilter` (dual)

### 3. Router Filter
The terminal decoder filter that forwards requests upstream. Explain:
- Route selection: how the router uses `RouteConfiguration` to pick a cluster
- How it obtains an HTTP connection pool from `ClusterManager`
- Upstream request lifecycle: `UpstreamRequest` creation, retry logic, timeout handling
- Shadow routing and hedged request support (if applicable)

### 4. Cluster Manager and Upstream Connectivity
The upstream connection pool and cluster management layer. Explain:
- How `ClusterManagerImpl` provides connection pools per cluster
- Load balancing: how the router obtains a host from the cluster's load balancer
- Connection pool mechanics: the relationship between logical connection pools and physical connections
- How health checking and outlier detection feed back into the load balancer

## Document Requirements

1. **Component Responsibilities** — what each component owns
2. **Data Flow** — the path of an HTTP request from downstream bytes to upstream dispatch, and the response path back
3. **Extension Points** — where users extend Envoy (HTTP filters, cluster extensions, load balancers, access loggers)
4. **Error Handling** — how errors at each stage (codec errors, filter errors, upstream failures) are handled
5. **relevant source files** — reference the actual source files in the envoyproxy/envoy repository

## Anti-Requirements

- Do NOT generate a simple API listing or header-file dump
- Do NOT fabricate class names or file paths that don't exist in the repository
- Do NOT cover Envoy components outside the HCM request path (e.g., xDS config delivery, listener management)


## Artifact-Only Evaluation

You are in **artifact-only mode**. Your workspace is empty — all code discovery
must go through Sourcegraph MCP tools. Express all code changes as **unified
diffs** in your output artifact (e.g., `fix_patch` fields in review.json, or a
standalone `solution.patch` file). Do NOT attempt to edit source files directly
— there are no source files in your workspace.

Perfect! I've created a comprehensive architecture document for Envoy's HTTP Connection Manager. The document is now available at `/workspace/documentation.md`.

## Document Summary

The architecture document covers all four required components and their interactions:

### **1. ConnectionManagerImpl** (lines 48-150)
- Implements `Network::ReadFilter` to receive raw bytes
- Manages connection lifecycle and creates `ActiveStream` objects
- Implements lazy codec instantiation (H1/H2 vs H3)
- Handles connection-level concerns: drain decisions, overload management, flow control

### **2. ActiveStream & FilterManager** (lines 152-330)
- **ActiveStream**: Per-stream container wrapping request/response pairs and owning the filter chain
- **FilterManager**: Filter chain execution engine with:
  - Decoder filters (forward order: A→B→C)
  - Encoder filters (reverse order: C→B→A)
  - Detailed explanation of filter iteration, buffering, and state management

### **3. Router Filter** (lines 332-530)
- Route selection using `RouteConfiguration`
- Host selection via load balancer
- Connection pool acquisition from `ClusterManager`
- `UpstreamRequest` creation for upstream lifecycle
- Retry logic, timeouts, and hedged requests

### **4. Cluster Manager & Upstream Connectivity** (lines 532-720)
- Cluster abstraction and load balancing algorithms
- HTTP connection pool mechanics (H1, H2, H3)
- Health checking and outlier detection
- Priority and locality-based routing

### **Key Sections**
- **Complete data flow diagrams** (lines 722-840) showing request arrival through upstream dispatch
- **Extension points** (lines 842-950) for HTTP filters, routes, load balancers, and tracing
- **Error handling** (lines 952-1010) for codec, filter, upstream, and resource limit errors
- **All relevant s

  "content": "# Envoy HTTP Connection Manager Architecture\n\n## Overview\n\nThe HTTP Connection Manager (HCM) is the central network filter in Envoy that processes HTTP traffic on a downstream connection. This document explains how the major components interact to receive HTTP requests on a downstream connection, process them through a filter chain, and dispatch them to upstream clusters.\n\nThe HCM architecture follows a clear separation of concerns:\n- **ConnectionManagerImpl**: Owns the downstream connection lifecycle and manages individual streams\n- **ActiveStream**: Wraps a single HTTP request/response pair and owns the filter chain\n- **FilterManager**: Executes the per-stream filter chain in both directions (decode and encode)\n- **Router Filter**: Terminal decoder filter that selects an upstream cluster and route\n- **UpstreamRequest & Cluster Manager**: Handle upstream connection pooling and host selection\n\n## 1. ConnectionManagerImpl: Connection Lifecycle and Stream Management\n\n### Responsibilities\n\n`ConnectionManagerImpl` (source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.h/.cc) is the entry point for HTTP processing. It implements three key interfaces:\n\n1. **Network::ReadFilter** \u2014 Receives raw bytes from the network layer\n2. **ServerConnectionCallbacks** \u2014 Receives decoded HTTP streams from the codec\n3. **Network::ConnectionCallbacks** \u2014 Handles connection lifecycle events (reset, close)\n\n### Key Features\n\n#### 1.1 Network Ingress: onData()\n\nWhen data arrives on a downstream connection:\n\n```cpp\nNetwork::FilterStatus ConnectionManagerImpl::onData(Buffer::Instance& data, bool end_stream)\n```\n\n- **Lazy codec instantiation**: The codec is created on first `onData()` call (or on `onConnection()` for H3/QUIC)\n  - HTTP/1.1 uses `Http1::CodecImpl`\n  - HTTP/2 uses `Http2::CodecImpl`\n  - HTTP/3 uses `QuicCodec`\n\n- The codec parses raw bytes and invokes `ServerConnectionCallbacks::newStream()` for each decoded HTTP message\n- The decoded data is buffered via a watermark buffer to manage backpressure\n\n#### 1.2 Stream Creation: newStream()\n\nWhen the codec detects a new HTTP request:\n\n```cpp\nRequestDecoder& ConnectionManagerImpl::newStream(ResponseEncoder& response_encoder,\n                                                bool is_internally_created = false)\n```\n\nThis creates an **ActiveStream** object that:\n- Wraps the request/response pair\n- Owns the FilterManager for this stream\n- Implements `RequestDecoder` to receive headers, data, and trailers from the codec\n- Implements `FilterManagerCallbacks` to send encoded response back to the codec\n\nEach `ActiveStream` is linked into a connection-wide list for lifecycle management.\n\n#### 1.3 Connection-Level Concerns\n\n**Drain decisions**: The `DrainDecision` interface checks if the connection should be drained (usually triggered by server shutdown). When draining:\n- Existing streams continue to completion\n- New streams may be rejected or drained immediately after completion\n- The connection closes once all streams are done\n\n**Overload management**: ConnectionManagerImpl integrates with Envoy's overload manager:\n- **HcmDecodeHeaders**: Can shed load by rejecting new streams\n- **HcmCodecCreation**: Can prevent new codec instantiation under extreme load\n- **DisableHttpKeepAlive**: Can force connections to close after each request\n\n**Flow control**: Watermark-based backpressure is propagated:\n- When upstream response buffers reach high watermark, downstream is paused\n- When upstream buffers drop below low watermark, downstream resumes\n- This prevents unbounded memory growth\n\n#### 1.4 Connection Lifecycle\n\n```\nonNewConnection()\n    \u2193\n[codec created on onData or onConnection]\n    \u2193\n[newStream() called for each HTTP message]\n    \u2193\n[ActiveStreams process requests concurrently]\n    \u2193\nonEvent(ConnectionEvent::LocalClose | RemoteClose)\n    \u2193\n[all ActiveStreams deferred-deleted, connection destroyed]\n```\n\n**Source files**:\n- Header: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.h` (lines 60-132)\n- Implementation: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc` (line 118+)\n\n---\n\n## 2. ActiveStream: Per-Stream Request/Response Container\n\n### Responsibilities\n\nAn `ActiveStream` (defined inside `ConnectionManagerImpl` at source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.h:141) wraps a single HTTP request/response pair and manages:\n\n1. **Codec event handling**: Receives headers, data, and trailers from the codec\n2. **Filter chain ownership**: Creates and owns the `FilterManager`\n3. **Stream-level state**: Timeouts, metadata, trailers, stream info\n4. **Response encoding**: Sends encoded response back to codec\n\n### Key Data Structures\n\n```cpp\nstruct ActiveStream : public RequestDecoder,\n                      public FilterManagerCallbacks,\n                      public DownstreamStreamFilterCallbacks,\n                      public CodecEventCallbacks {\n  // Request headers received from downstream\n  RequestHeaderMapSharedPtr request_headers_;\n\n  // Response information\n  ResponseHeaderMapPtr response_headers_;\n  ResponseTrailerMapPtr response_trailers_;\n  ResponseHeaderMapPtr informational_headers_;  // 1xx informational responses\n\n  // Filter chain\n  FilterManager filter_manager_;\n\n  // Stream metadata\n  StreamInfo::StreamInfoImpl stream_info_;\n  uint64_t stream_id_;\n\n  // State tracking\n  struct State {\n    bool codec_saw_local_complete_;     // Response sent to codec\n    bool codec_encode_complete_;        // Codec finished encoding\n    bool on_reset_stream_called_;       // Stream was reset\n    bool is_zombie_stream_;             // Waiting for codec cleanup\n    // ... other flags ...\n  } state_;\n};\n```\n\n### Request Processing Path\n\n**Phase 1: Headers**\n```cpp\nvoid ActiveStream::decodeHeaders(RequestHeaderMapSharedPtr&& headers, bool end_stream)\n```\n- Headers are stored in `request_headers_`\n- Stream info is initialized with request details\n- Headers are passed to `FilterManager::decodeHeaders()` to iterate through decoder filters\n- Router filter (terminal decoder filter) is invoked last\n\n**Phase 2: Body Data**\n```cpp\nvoid ActiveStream::decodeData(Buffer::Instance& data, bool end_stream)\n```\n- Data is passed to `FilterManager::decodeData()` for decoder filters\n- Each filter can buffer, modify, or forward data\n- Router filter eventually sends data to upstream\n\n**Phase 3: Trailers**\n```cpp\nvoid ActiveStream::decodeTrailers(RequestTrailerMapPtr&& trailers)\n```\n- Trailers are passed through `FilterManager::decodeTrailers()`\n- Indicates end of request body\n\n### Response Encoding Path\n\nWhen response arrives from upstream (via router filter \u2192 upstream response):\n\n**Phase 1: Response Headers**\n```cpp\nvoid ActiveStream::encodeHeaders(ResponseHeaderMap& response_headers, bool end_stream)\n```\n- Headers go through encoder filter chain (in reverse order)\n- Are finalized and passed to codec for encoding\n\n**Phase 2: Response Data**\n```cpp\nvoid ActiveStream::encodeData(Buffer::Instance& data, bool end_stream)\n```\n- Response body data is encoded and sent downstream\n\n**Phase 3: Response Trailers**\n```cpp\nvoid ActiveStream::encodeTrailers(ResponseTrailerMap& trailers)\n```\n- Trailers complete the response\n\n### Stream-Level Concerns\n\n**Timeouts**:\n- **Request timeout**: How long to wait for request to arrive from downstream\n- **Duration timeout**: Maximum time from request headers to response headers\n- **Idle timeout**: Inactivity timeout\n\n**Tracing**: Each stream has a `Tracing::Span` that can be started by the tracer\n\n**Access logging**: Combined from both connection-level and filter-level access log handlers\n\n**Source files**:\n- `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.h` (lines 141-450)\n- `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc` (stream processing methods)\n\n---\n\n## 3. FilterManager and the HTTP Filter Chain\n\n### Responsibilities\n\n`FilterManager` (source/common/http/filter_manager.h/.cc) is the per-stream filter chain execution engine. It:\n\n1. Creates filter instances via `FilterChainFactory`\n2. Manages decoder and encoder filter chains\n3. Iterates through filters in the correct order\n4. Handles filter return statuses (Continue, StopIteration, SendLocalReply, etc.)\n5. Buffers data when filters stop iteration\n6. Manages per-filter state and watermarks\n\n### Filter Chain Structure\n\nFilters are organized in two chains:\n\n```cpp\nstruct StreamDecoderFilters {\n  std::vector<ActiveStreamDecoderFilterPtr> entries_;\n  // Iterates forward: filter[0], filter[1], ..., filter[N]\n};\n\nstruct StreamEncoderFilters {\n  std::vector<ActiveStreamEncoderFilterPtr> entries_;\n  // Iterates reverse: filter[N], ..., filter[1], filter[0]\n};\n```\n\n**Why reverse iteration for encoders?**\n\nIf filters are configured as: `[A, B, C]`\n- **Decoder**: A \u2192 B \u2192 C (request flows forward)\n- **Encoder**: C \u2192 B \u2192 A (response flows backward, last decoder to respond first)\n\nThis allows filters to see the response in the reverse order they saw the request.\n\n### Request Path: Decoder Filter Chain\n\n```\n[Downstream]\n     \u2193\n[Router reads headers from downstream]\n     \u2193\nActiveStream::decodeHeaders()\n     \u2193\nFilterManager::decodeHeaders()\n     \u2193\nFilter[0]::decodeHeaders()\n     \u2193\nFilter[1]::decodeHeaders()\n     \u2193\nFilter[N]::decodeHeaders() [Router Filter - terminal filter]\n     \u2193\n[Route selected, upstream pool acquired]\n     \u2193\nRouter creates UpstreamRequest\n```\n\nEach filter receives the status from `decodeHeaders()`:\n\n```cpp\nenum class FilterHeadersStatus {\n  Continue,              // Continue to next filter\n  StopIteration,         // Stop but don't buffer\n  StopAllIteration,      // Stop and buffer subsequent frames\n  ContinueAndEndStream,  // Continue but signal end\n  // ...\n};\n```\n\n- If a filter returns `StopAllIteration`, the FilterManager buffers any subsequent data/trailers\n- When the filter calls `continueDecoding()`, iteration resumes from that filter\n\n**Data frame processing**:\n\n```cpp\nFilterManager::decodeData(Buffer::Instance& data, bool end_stream)\n```\n\nData flows through the same filter chain. Filters can:\n- Modify the buffer in-place\n- Replace the entire buffer\n- Buffer data internally and consume it\n- Pass data through unchanged\n\n**Trailers**:\n\n```cpp\nFilterManager::decodeTrailers(RequestTrailerMapPtr&& trailers)\n```\n\nTrailers complete the request body and flow through decoders in the same order.\n\n### Response Path: Encoder Filter Chain\n\nWhen response arrives from upstream:\n\n```\n[Upstream Response arrives]\n     \u2193\nUpstreamRequest::decodeHeaders() [receives upstream 200 OK]\n     \u2193\nRouter Filter internal processing\n     \u2193\nRouter invokes FilterManager::encodeHeaders() [backward through filter chain]\n     \u2193\nFilter[N-1]::encodeHeaders()\n     \u2193\nFilter[1]::encodeHeaders()\n     \u2193\nFilter[0]::encodeHeaders()\n     \u2193\nActiveStream::encodeHeaders() [sends to codec]\n     \u2193\n[Codec encodes and sends downstream]\n```\n\nEncoder filters work similarly to decoder filters but in reverse order.\n\n### Filter Callbacks and State Management\n\nFilters can access stream information and control flow:\n\n```cpp\n// From StreamFilterCallbacks interface\nclass StreamFilterCallbacks {\npublic:\n  OptRef<const Network::Connection> connection();\n  Router::RouteConstSharedPtr route();\n  void resetStream(Http::StreamResetReason reason,\n                   absl::string_view transport_failure_reason);\n  Upstream::ClusterInfoConstSharedPtr clusterInfo();\n  StreamInfo::StreamInfo& streamInfo();\n\n  // Access headers\n  RequestHeaderMapOptRef requestHeaders();\n  ResponseHeaderMapOptRef responseHeaders();\n};\n```\n\n### Watermark Buffering\n\nWhen a filter calls `setBufferLimit()`, FilterManager enforces memory limits:\n\n```cpp\nvoid setBufferLimit(uint64_t limit);\n```\n\nIf buffered data exceeds this limit:\n- Watermark callback triggers\n- Upstream reading is disabled\n- Data stops flowing until buffer drains\n\n### Local Replies\n\nA filter can generate a local reply without contacting upstream:\n\n```cpp\nvoid FilterManager::sendLocalReply(\n    Code code,\n    absl::string_view body,\n    const std::function<void(ResponseHeaderMap& headers)>& modify_headers,\n    const absl::optional<Grpc::Status::GrpcStatus> grpc_status,\n    absl::string_view details)\n```\n\nThis causes:\n- All decoder filters to be skipped for this stream\n- Response headers/body to be created locally\n- Response to flow through encoder filters\n- Stream to complete without upstream contact\n\n### Match-Based Filter Configuration\n\nFilterManager supports dynamic filter configuration via matchers. Filters can have:\n- **Route-specific config**: Set by router based on matched route\n- **Match tree config**: Set based on request/response matching\n\n**Source files**:\n- Header: `source/common/http/filter_manager.h` (lines 34-250)\n- Implementation: `source/common/http/filter_manager.cc` (filter chain iteration)\n- FilterChainFactory: `source/common/http/conn_manager_config.h` (calls `createFilterChain()`)\n\n---\n\n## 4. Router Filter: Route Selection and Upstream Dispatch\n\n### Responsibilities\n\nThe Router Filter (source/common/router/router.h/.cc) is the terminal decoder filter that:\n\n1. Selects a route from `RouteConfiguration`\n2. Obtains a load balanced upstream host\n3. Gets (or creates) an HTTP connection pool for that host\n4. Creates an `UpstreamRequest` to forward the request\n5. Handles retries, timeouts, and request hedging\n6. Processes upstream response and sends it back through encoder filters\n\n### Route Selection\n\n**Route Selection Process**:\n\n```cpp\nHttp::FilterHeadersStatus Filter::decodeHeaders(\n    Http::RequestHeaderMap& headers, bool end_stream)\n```\n\n1. **Find cluster**: The router uses the decoded headers to find a matching route:\n   ```cpp\n   RouteConstSharedPtr route = decoder_callbacks_->route();\n   ```\n   Route selection uses:\n   - Request path (prefix, exact, or regex match)\n   - Request headers\n   - Virtual host match\n   - Scoped routing configuration (if configured)\n\n2. **Extract route entry**: From the matched route, get the RouteEntry:\n   ```cpp\n   RouteEntryConstSharedPtr route_entry = route->routeEntry();\n   ```\n\n3. **Select cluster**: Each route entry specifies a cluster:\n   ```cpp\n   absl::string_view cluster_name = route_entry->clusterName();\n   ```\n\n4. **Get cluster**: From the ClusterManager:\n   ```cpp\n   Upstream::ThreadLocalCluster* cluster =\n       config_->cm_.getThreadLocalCluster(cluster_name);\n   ```\n\n### Host Selection and Connection Pool\n\nOnce a cluster is selected:\n\n```cpp\n// Get load balancer from the cluster\nauto load_balancer = cluster->loadBalancer();\n\n// Select a host using load balancing algorithm\nUpstream::HostConstSharedPtr host =\n    load_balancer.chooseHost(load_balancer_context);\n```\n\nThe `LoadBalancerContext` includes:\n- Request headers (for header-based routing)\n- Stream info\n- Connection cookies (for session affinity)\n- Hash key (for consistent hashing)\n\nOnce a host is selected:\n\n```cpp\n// Get the HTTP connection pool for this host\nHttp::ConnectionPool::Instance* pool =\n    cluster->httpConnPool(host, route_entry->upstreamOptions());\n```\n\nThe connection pool is responsible for:\n- Creating TCP connections to the upstream host\n- Multiplexing multiple requests over a single connection (H2, H3)\n- Managing connection lifetime and reuse\n- Connection health state\n\n### Upstream Request Creation\n\nOnce a pool is obtained:\n\n```cpp\nupstream_request_ = std::make_unique<UpstreamRequest>(\n    *this,                  // RouterFilterInterface (parent)\n    std::move(conn_pool),   // HTTP connection pool\n    can_send_early_data,\n    can_use_http3,\n    enable_half_close);\n```\n\n### Request Forwarding\n\nThe router forwards request data to the upstream request:\n\n**Headers**:\n```cpp\nFilter::decodeHeaders() \u2192 UpstreamRequest::acceptHeadersFromRouter()\n```\n\n**Body data**:\n```cpp\nFilter::decodeData() \u2192 UpstreamRequest::acceptDataFromRouter()\n```\n\n**Trailers**:\n```cpp\nFilter::decodeTrailers() \u2192 UpstreamRequest::acceptTrailersFromRouter()\n```\n\nThe UpstreamRequest buffers data until an upstream connection is established, then sends it.\n\n### Timeout Management\n\nThe router sets up several timeout timers:\n\n**Request timeout**: Maximum time to wait for complete request\n```cpp\nvoid setupRequestTimeout();\n```\n\n**Response timeout** (per-try): Maximum time to receive response\n```cpp\nvoid setupPerTryTimeout();\n```\n\n**Total timeout**: Maximum time from request start to response complete\n\nIf a timeout fires:\n- Stream is reset\n- Local reply is sent (e.g., 504 Gateway Timeout)\n- Retry logic may kick in (if configured)\n\n### Retry Logic\n\nIf upstream returns an error or times out:\n\n```cpp\nif (shouldRetry(upstream_response, retry_policy)) {\n  retry_attempts_++;\n  resetUpstream();\n  selectUpstreamHost();  // Possibly different host\n  // Retry with new upstream\n}\n```\n\nRetry conditions include:\n- 5xx errors (if retry policy allows)\n- Connection reset\n- Per-try timeout (if retries are available)\n\n### Hedged Requests\n\nIf hedging is enabled:\n\n```cpp\nif (should_hedge) {\n  // Start a new upstream request in parallel with the first one\n  hedged_upstream_requests_.push_back(\n      std::make_unique<UpstreamRequest>(...));\n}\n```\n\nThe first response to arrive wins; others are cancelled.\n\n### Shadow Routing\n\nIf the route specifies a shadow policy:\n\n```cpp\nif (route_entry->shadowPolicy().cluster() != \"\") {\n  // Send a copy of the request to the shadow cluster\n  shadow_request_ = std::make_unique<UpstreamRequest>(...);\n  // Shadow response is logged but not sent downstream\n}\n```\n\n### Response Processing\n\nWhen upstream sends response:\n\n```cpp\nvoid UpstreamRequest::decodeHeaders(\n    Http::ResponseHeaderMapPtr&& headers,\n    bool end_stream)\n```\n\nThe upstream request:\n1. Passes headers to router filter\n2. Router filter invokes encoder filters\n3. Response flows back down through encoder chain\n4. ActiveStream::encodeHeaders() sends to codec\n\n**Source files**:\n- Header: `source/common/router/router.h` (lines 298-450)\n- Implementation: `source/common/router/router.cc` (lines 64+)\n- UpstreamRequest: `source/common/router/upstream_request.h` (lines 67+)\n\n---\n\n## 5. UpstreamRequest: Upstream Connection Lifecycle\n\n### Responsibilities\n\n`UpstreamRequest` (source/common/router/upstream_request.h/.cc) manages the lifecycle of a single upstream HTTP request:\n\n1. Acquires a connection from the pool\n2. Buffers downstream data until connection is ready\n3. Sends request to upstream\n4. Receives and processes upstream response\n5. Handles per-try timeouts and retries\n6. Manages flow control between downstream and upstream\n\n### Connection Pool Interface\n\nThe UpstreamRequest calls the HTTP connection pool:\n\n```cpp\nclass Http::ConnectionPool::Instance {\npublic:\n  // Request a new stream from the pool\n  Cancellable* newStream(\n      Http::ResponseDecoder& response_decoder,\n      Http::ConnectionPool::Callbacks& callbacks,\n      const StreamOptions& options);\n};\n```\n\nThe pool returns a `Cancellable` that can be used to cancel the request if needed.\n\n### Pool Callbacks\n\nWhen the pool acquires a connection:\n\n```cpp\nvoid UpstreamRequest::onPoolReady(\n    std::unique_ptr<GenericUpstream>&& upstream,\n    Upstream::HostDescriptionConstSharedPtr host,\n    const Network::ConnectionInfoProvider& address_provider,\n    StreamInfo::StreamInfo& info,\n    absl::optional<Http::Protocol> protocol)\n```\n\nThe pool provides:\n- A `GenericUpstream` object (codec wrapper for the upstream connection)\n- The selected host information\n- The actual protocol negotiated (H2, H3, etc.)\n\n### Data Buffering\n\nRequest data is buffered while waiting for upstream connection:\n\n```cpp\nvoid UpstreamRequest::acceptDataFromRouter(Buffer::Instance& data, bool end_stream)\n```\n\nIf the upstream connection isn't ready:\n- Data is buffered in `upstream_buffer_`\n- Backpressure is applied to the router filter via watermarks\n\nOnce connection is ready:\n- Buffered data is flushed to upstream\n- New data flows directly through\n\n### Per-Try Timeout\n\nEach upstream attempt has its own timeout:\n\n```cpp\nvoid UpstreamRequest::setupPerTryTimeout()\n```\n\nIf the upstream doesn't respond within this timeout:\n- Upstream connection is reset\n- Retry logic is triggered (if allowed)\n- Or local 504 reply is sent\n\n### Per-Try Codec Filter Chain\n\nThe upstream request can have its own HTTP filter chain for transforming upstream request/response:\n\n```cpp\nstd::unique_ptr<UpstreamFilterManager> upstream_filter_manager_;\n```\n\nThese filters allow transforming the request before sending upstream (e.g., adding headers) or transforming the response before sending downstream.\n\n### Watermark Management\n\nUpstreamRequest manages flow control:\n\n```cpp\nstruct DownstreamWatermarkManager : Http::DownstreamWatermarkCallbacks {\n  // Called when response buffer exceeds high watermark\n  void onAboveWriteBufferHighWatermark();\n\n  // Called when response buffer drops below low watermark\n  void onBelowWriteBufferLowWatermark();\n};\n```\n\nThis pauses/resumes downstream reading when upstream response buffer fills up.\n\n### Reset and Cleanup\n\nIf the upstream connection fails or is reset:\n\n```cpp\nvoid UpstreamRequest::onResetStream(\n    Http::StreamResetReason reason,\n    absl::string_view transport_failure_reason)\n```\n\nThe router filter can decide to:\n- Retry with a different host\n- Send a local reply (e.g., 503 Service Unavailable)\n- Reset the downstream stream\n\n**Source files**:\n- Header: `source/common/router/upstream_request.h` (lines 67-250)\n- Implementation: `source/common/router/upstream_request.cc`\n\n---\n\n## 6. Cluster Manager and Upstream Connectivity\n\n### Responsibilities\n\n`ClusterManagerImpl` (source/common/upstream/cluster_manager_impl.h/.cc) provides:\n\n1. **Cluster management**: Creates and manages cluster objects from configuration\n2. **Connection pooling**: Provides per-host HTTP connection pools\n3. **Load balancing**: Returns hosts to connect to\n4. **Health checking**: Tracks endpoint health\n5. **Outlier detection**: Removes unhealthy hosts\n\n### Cluster Abstraction\n\nA cluster represents a logical group of upstream endpoints:\n\n```cpp\nclass Cluster {\npublic:\n  // Load balancing\n  LoadBalancer& loadBalancer();\n\n  // Connection pool\n  Http::ConnectionPool::Instance* httpConnPool(\n      Upstream::HostConstSharedPtr host,\n      const Http::HttpConnectionPoolOptions& options);\n\n  // Health/monitoring\n  Health::HealthChecker* healthChecker();\n  Outlier::OutlierDetector* outlierDetector();\n};\n```\n\n### Load Balancer Selection\n\nThe cluster has a load balancer that selects hosts:\n\n```cpp\nclass LoadBalancer {\npublic:\n  // Select a host based on context\n  ChooseHostStatus chooseHost(LoadBalancerContext* context);\n};\n```\n\nDifferent load balancing algorithms:\n- **Round Robin**: Cycles through all healthy hosts\n- **Least Request**: Selects host with fewest active requests\n- **Ring Hash**: Consistent hashing for session affinity\n- **Random**: Random selection\n- **Maglev**: Another consistent hashing algorithm\n\nThe context provides:\n- Request headers\n- Hash key (if using hash-based LB)\n- Priority (for multi-priority routing)\n- Cookies (for session affinity)\n\n### Connection Pool Structure\n\nEach host has a connection pool:\n\n```cpp\nclass HttpConnPoolImplBase : public Http::ConnectionPool::Instance {\npublic:\n  // Request a new stream\n  Cancellable* newStream(ResponseDecoder& decoder, Callbacks& callbacks);\n\n  // Connection management\n  void drainConnections();\n  bool hasActiveConnections();\n};\n```\n\n**For HTTP/1.1**:\n- One physical TCP connection per stream (multiplexing not supported)\n- Pool maintains a queue of pending requests\n- When a connection completes, next pending request uses it\n\n**For HTTP/2**:\n- Multiple streams share a single TCP connection\n- Pool creates up to `max_connections` physical connections\n- Streams are multiplexed across these connections\n- Each connection can handle many concurrent streams\n\n**For HTTP/3/QUIC**:\n- Similar to HTTP/2 but over UDP/QUIC\n- Better connection establishment latency\n\n### Active Client (Physical Connection)\n\nEach physical connection is managed by an `ActiveClient`:\n\n```cpp\nclass ActiveClient : public GenericUpstream {\npublic:\n  // Send headers/data/trailers to upstream\n  void sendHeaders(RequestHeaderMap& headers, bool end_stream);\n  void sendData(Buffer::Instance& data, bool end_stream);\n\n  // Codec for encoding/decoding\n  CodecClient& codec();\n};\n```\n\nThe pool manages:\n- Creating new ActiveClients when needed\n- Reusing idle ActiveClients for new requests\n- Removing unhealthy ActiveClients\n- Enforcing connection limits\n\n### Health Checking\n\nIf health checking is configured for a cluster:\n\n```cpp\nHealth::HealthChecker* health_checker = cluster->healthChecker();\n```\n\nHealth checkers periodically probe endpoints (via HTTP or other protocol) and mark hosts as healthy/unhealthy. The load balancer only sends traffic to healthy hosts.\n\n### Outlier Detection\n\nIf outlier detection is enabled:\n\n```cpp\nOutlier::OutlierDetector* detector = cluster->outlierDetector();\n```\n\nThe detector tracks:\n- Request latencies\n- Error rates\n- Consecutive errors\n\nIf a host exceeds thresholds, it's temporarily removed from load balancing (ejected). After a recovery timeout, it's re-enabled.\n\n### Priority and Locality-Based Routing\n\nClusters support multi-tier load balancing:\n\n```cpp\nenum class Priority {\n  Primary = 0,    // Try primary endpoints first\n  Secondary = 1,  // Fall back to secondary if primary exhausted\n};\n```\n\nEach priority level has endpoints in different localities. The load balancer:\n- Tries primary priority first\n- Falls back to secondary if all primary unhealthy\n- Within a priority, may prefer endpoints in the local zone\n\n**Source files**:\n- Header: `source/common/upstream/cluster_manager_impl.h` (lines 52-250)\n- Implementation: `source/common/upstream/cluster_manager_impl.cc`\n- Cluster abstraction: `source/common/upstream/upstream_impl.h`\n\n---\n\n## Data Flow: Request Arrival to Upstream Dispatch\n\n### Complete Request Path\n\n```\n\u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510\n\u2502 DOWNSTREAM CONNECTION ESTABLISHED                             \u2502\n\u2514\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2518\n                           \u2193\n\u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510\n\u2502 ConnectionManagerImpl::onNewConnection()                       \u2502\n\u2502 - Extension Points\n\n### 1. HTTP Filters\n\nUsers extend Envoy by implementing HTTP filters:\n\n```cpp\nclass StreamDecoderFilter {\npublic:\n  virtual FilterHeadersStatus decodeHeaders(\n      RequestHeaderMap& headers, bool end_stream);\n  virtual FilterDataStatus decodeData(\n      Buffer::Instance& data, bool end_stream);\n  virtual FilterTrailersStatus decodeTrailers(\n      RequestTrailerMap& trailers);\n  virtual void setDecoderFilterCallbacks(StreamDecoderFilterCallbacks&);\n};\n\nclass StreamEncoderFilter {\npublic:\n  virtual Filter1xxHeadersStatus encode1xxHeaders(ResponseHeaderMap&);\n  virtual FilterHeadersStatus encodeHeaders(\n      ResponseHeaderMap& headers, bool end_stream);\n  virtual FilterDataStatus encodeData(\n      Buffer::Instance& data, bool end_stream);\n  virtual FilterTrailersStatus encodeTrailers(\n      ResponseTrailerMap& trailers);\n  virtual void setEncoderFilterCallbacks(StreamEncoderFilterCallbacks&);\n};\n```\n\n**Extension points for filters**:\n- Inspect/modify request headers (e.g., add trace headers)\n- Inspect/buffer request data (e.g., for WAF)\n- Generate local replies (e.g., authentication)\n- Inspect/modify response headers (e.g., add CORS headers)\n- Access route/cluster info via callbacks\n- Implement custom routing logic via match trees\n\n**Built-in filters** (in order):\n- Microversion filter\n- Router filter (terminal decoder filter)\n- Access log filter\n\n### 2. Route Selection\n\nRoutes are configured via `RouteConfiguration` and can be:\n\n```cpp\nclass RouteEntry {\npublic:\n  // Matching criteria\n  virtual bool pathMatchCriterion(...);\n  virtual absl::optional<StringMatcher> hostPattern();\n\n  // Route actions\n  virtual absl::string_view clusterName();\n  virtual TimeoutData timeout();\n  virtual const RetryPolicy& retryPolicy();\n  virtual bool shadowPolicy();\n};\n```\n\nUsers can:\n- Define static routes in bootstrap config\n- Use RDS (Route Discovery Service) for dynamic routing\n- Use weighted clusters for canary deployments\n- Use retry policies and request hedging\n- Use shadow routing for testing\n\n### 3. Load Balancing\n\nUsers can implement custom load balancers:\n\n```cpp\nclass LoadBalancer {\npublic:\n  virtual ChooseHostStatus chooseHost(LoadBalancerContext* context);\n};\n```\n\nCustom load balancers can:\n- Access request headers from context\n- Use hash keys for consistent hashing\n- Implement custom affinity logic\n- Apply custom weighting schemes\n\n**Built-in LBs**:\n- Round Robin\n- Least Request\n- Ring Hash\n- Maglev Hash\n- Random\n- Weighted Cluster\n\n### 4. Cluster Extensions\n\nClusters support custom implementations:\n\n```cpp\nclass Cluster {\npublic:\n  virtual LoadBalancer& loadBalancer();\n  virtual Http::ConnectionPool::Instance* httpConnPool(...);\n  virtual HealthChecker* healthChecker();\n  virtual OutlierDetector* outlierDetector();\n};\n```\n\nUsers can implement:\n- Custom health checkers (beyond HTTP probes)\n- Custom connection pool implementations\n- Custom outlier detection algorithms\n- Custom load balancer factories\n\n### 5. Access Logging\n\nAccess logs are configured per stream and can use various sinks and formats:\n\n```cpp\nclass AccessLog {\npublic:\n  virtual void log(const RequestHeaderMap* request_headers,\n                   const ResponseHeaderMap* response_headers,\n                   const ResponseTrailerMap* response_trailers,\n                   const StreamInfo& stream_info);\n};\n```\n\nUsers can:\n- Log to file, syslog, or custom sink\n- Use built-in formatters or custom formatters\n- Apply sampling or conditional logging\n- Access detailed stream info (timings, response codes, etc.)\n\n### 6. Tracing\n\nIf tracing is configured, each stream has a `Tracing::Span`:\n\n```cpp\nclass Tracer {\npublic:\n  virtual SpanPtr startSpan(const Config& config, ...);\n};\n```\n\nSpans are created at:\n- Request ingress (if configured)\n- Per operation (if router specifies operation name)\n- Per upstream request (if enabled)\n\nUsers can integrate with:\n- Jaeger\n- Zipkin\n- Datadog\n- Custom tracers\n\n---\n\n## Error Handling\n\n### Downstream Errors\n\n**Codec errors**: If the codec fails to parse HTTP (invalid headers, etc.):\n- Connection is closed\n- Partial streams are reset\n- `http_connection_errors` counter incremented\n\n**Filter errors**: If a filter returns an error or calls `resetStream()`:\n- All downstream and upstream resources are cleaned up\n- Connection may remain open for other streams\n- Access log is generated\n\n**Local replies**: If a filter generates a local reply (no upstream):\n- Reply flows through remaining encoder filters\n- Codec encodes response\n- Connection remains open\n\n### Upstream Errors\n\n**Pool failures**: If the HTTP connection pool can't acquire a connection:\n- Router filter invokes retry logic (if configured)\n- Or sends local 503 Service Unavailable\n- Stream completes with error flags in stream info\n\n**Upstream reset**: If upstream closes the connection:\n- UpstreamRequest detects reset\n- Router filter decides whether to retry\n- Or forwards reset to downstream (triggers downstream reset)\n\n**Per-try timeout**: If per-try timeout fires:\n- UpstreamRequest is reset\n- Router retries (if allowed)\n- Or sends local 504 Gateway Timeout\n\n**Upstream 5xx**: If upstream returns 5xx error:\n- Router checks retry policy\n- If retryable and retries available, retries with different host\n- Or forwards 5xx to downstream\n\n### Resource Limits\n\n**Overload handling**: During overload:\n- `HcmDecodeHeaders` shed point can reject new streams\n- `HcmCodecCreation` shed point can prevent codec instantiation\n- `StopAcceptingRequests` can reject all new requests\n- `DisableHttpKeepAlive` forces connection closure after each request\n\n**Watermark backpressure**: When buffers fill:\n- Upstream reading is paused\n- Downstream is paused via connection watermarks\n- Flow resumes when buffers drain\n\n---\n\n## Summary\n\nThe HTTP Connection Manager implements a clean, composable architecture:\n\n1. **ConnectionManagerImpl** owns the downstream connection and creates streams\n2. **ActiveStream** wraps each request/response and owns the filter chain\n3. **FilterManager** executes the filter chain in both directions\n4. **Router Filter** is the terminal decoder that selects upstream and creates UpstreamRequest\n5. **UpstreamRequest** manages the upstream connection and bridges upstream response back\n6. **ClusterManager** provides connection pools and host selection\n\nThis design allows:\n- **Extensibility**: Custom filters can inspect/modify requests and responses\n- **Composability**: Filters are independent and can be mixed and matched\n- **Efficiency**: Multiplexed connections (H2/H3) and lazy initialization reduce overhead\n- **Observability**: Detailed stream info, tracing, and access logs at each stage\n- **Resilience**: Retries, timeouts, health checking, and outlier detection\n\nThe architecture clearly separates concerns: network/codec handling, filter chain execution, routing/load balancing, and connection pooling. Each component has well-defined responsibilities and interfaces, making it straightforward to understand and extend Envoy's HTTP processing.\n",
  "file_path": "/workspace/documentation.md"

{
  "content": "# Envoy HTTP Connection Manager Architecture\n\n## Overview\n\nThe HTTP Connection Manager (HCM) is the central network filter in Envoy that processes HTTP traffic on a downstream connection. This document explains how the major components interact to receive HTTP requests on a downstream connection, process them through a filter chain, and dispatch them to upstream clusters.\n\nThe HCM architecture follows a clear separation of concerns:\n- **ConnectionManagerImpl**: Owns the downstream connection lifecycle and manages individual streams\n- **ActiveStream**: Wraps a single HTTP request/response pair and owns the filter chain\n- **FilterManager**: Executes the per-stream filter chain in both directions (decode and encode)\n- **Router Filter**: Terminal decoder filter that selects an upstream cluster and route\n- **UpstreamRequest & Cluster Manager**: Handle upstream connection pooling and host selection\n\n## 1. ConnectionManagerImpl: Connection Lifecycle and Stream Management\n\n### Responsibilities\n\n`ConnectionManagerImpl` (source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.h/.cc) is the entry point for HTTP processing. It implements three key interfaces:\n\n1. **Network::ReadFilter** \u2014 Receives raw bytes from the network layer\n2. **ServerConnectionCallbacks** \u2014 Receives decoded HTTP streams from the codec\n3. **Network::ConnectionCallbacks** \u2014 Handles connection lifecycle events (reset, close)\n\n### Key Features\n\n#### 1.1 Network Ingress: onData()\n\nWhen data arrives on a downstream connection:\n\n```cpp\nNetwork::FilterStatus ConnectionManagerImpl::onData(Buffer::Instance& data, bool end_stream)\n```\n\n- **Lazy codec instantiation**: The codec is created on first `onData()` call (or on `onConnection()` for H3/QUIC)\n  - HTTP/1.1 uses `Http1::CodecImpl`\n  - HTTP/2 uses `Http2::CodecImpl`\n  - HTTP/3 uses `QuicCodec`\n\n- The codec parses raw bytes and invokes `ServerConnectionCallbacks::newStream()` for each decoded HTTP message\n- The decoded data is buffered via a watermark buffer to manage backpressure\n\n#### 1.2 Stream Creation: newStream()\n\nWhen the codec detects a new HTTP request:\n\n```cpp\nRequestDecoder& ConnectionManagerImpl::newStream(ResponseEncoder& response_encoder,\n                                                bool is_internally_created = false)\n```\n\nThis creates an **ActiveStream** object that:\n- Wraps the request/response pair\n- Owns the FilterManager for this stream\n- Implements `RequestDecoder` to receive headers, data, and trailers from the codec\n- Implements `FilterManagerCallbacks` to send encoded response back to the codec\n\nEach `ActiveStream` is linked into a connection-wide list for lifecycle management.\n\n#### 1.3 Connection-Level Concerns\n\n**Drain decisions**: The `DrainDecision` interface checks if the connection should be drained (usually triggered by server shutdown). When draining:\n- Existing streams continue to completion\n- New streams may be rejected or drained immediately after completion\n- The connection closes once all streams are done\n\n**Overload management**: ConnectionManagerImpl integrates with Envoy's overload manager:\n- **HcmDecodeHeaders**: Can shed load by rejecting new streams\n- **HcmCodecCreation**: Can prevent new codec instantiation under extreme load\n- **DisableHttpKeepAlive**: Can force connections to close after each request\n\n**Flow control**: Watermark-based backpressure is propagated:\n- When upstream response buffers reach high watermark, downstream is paused\n- When upstream buffers drop below low watermark, downstream resumes\n- This prevents unbounded memory growth\n\n#### 1.4 Connection Lifecycle\n\n```\nonNewConnection()\n    \u2193\n[codec created on onData or onConnection]\n    \u2193\n[newStream() called for each HTTP message]\n    \u2193\n[ActiveStreams process requests concurrently]\n    \u2193\nonEvent(ConnectionEvent::LocalClose | RemoteClose)\n    \u2193\n[all ActiveStreams deferred-deleted, connection destroyed]\n```\n\n**Source files**:\n- Header: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.h` (lines 60-132)\n- Implementation: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc` (line 118+)\n\n---\n\n## 2. ActiveStream: Per-Stream Request/Response Container\n\n### Responsibilities\n\nAn `ActiveStream` (defined inside `ConnectionManagerImpl` at source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.h:141) wraps a single HTTP request/response pair and manages:\n\n1. **Codec event handling**: Receives headers, data, and trailers from the codec\n2. **Filter chain ownership**: Creates and owns the `FilterManager`\n3. **Stream-level state**: Timeouts, metadata, trailers, stream info\n4. **Response encoding**: Sends encoded response back to codec\n\n### Key Data Structures\n\n```cpp\nstruct ActiveStream : public RequestDecoder,\n                      public FilterManagerCallbacks,\n                      public DownstreamStreamFilterCallbacks,\n                      public CodecEventCallbacks {\n  // Request headers received from downstream\n  RequestHeaderMapSharedPtr request_headers_;\n\n  // Response information\n  ResponseHeaderMapPtr response_headers_;\n  ResponseTrailerMapPtr response_trailers_;\n  ResponseHeaderMapPtr informational_headers_;  // 1xx informational responses\n\n  // Filter chain\n  FilterManager filter_manager_;\n\n  // Stream metadata\n  StreamInfo::StreamInfoImpl stream_info_;\n  uint64_t stream_id_;\n\n  // State tracking\n  struct State {\n    bool codec_saw_local_complete_;     // Response sent to codec\n    bool codec_encode_complete_;        // Codec finished encoding\n    bool on_reset_stream_called_;       // Stream was reset\n    bool is_zombie_stream_;             // Waiting for codec cleanup\n    // ... other flags ...\n  } state_;\n};\n```\n\n### Request Processing Path\n\n**Phase 1: Headers**\n```cpp\nvoid ActiveStream::decodeHeaders(RequestHeaderMapSharedPtr&& headers, bool end_stream)\n```\n- Headers are stored in `request_headers_`\n- Stream info is initialized with request details\n- Headers are passed to `FilterManager::decodeHeaders()` to iterate through decoder filters\n- Router filter (terminal decoder filter) is invoked last\n\n**Phase 2: Body Data**\n```cpp\nvoid ActiveStream::decodeData(Buffer::Instance& data, bool end_stream)\n```\n- Data is passed to `FilterManager::decodeData()` for decoder filters\n- Each filter can buffer, modify, or forward data\n- Router filter eventually sends data to upstream\n\n**Phase 3: Trailers**\n```cpp\nvoid ActiveStream::decodeTrailers(RequestTrailerMapPtr&& trailers)\n```\n- Trailers are passed through `FilterManager::decodeTrailers()`\n- Indicates end of request body\n\n### Response Encoding Path\n\nWhen response arrives from upstream (via router filter \u2192 upstream response):\n\n**Phase 1: Response Headers**\n```cpp\nvoid ActiveStream::encodeHeaders(ResponseHeaderMap& response_headers, bool end_stream)\n```\n- Headers go through encoder filter chain (in reverse order)\n- Are finalized and passed to codec for encoding\n\n**Phase 2: Response Data**\n```cpp\nvoid ActiveStream::encodeData(Buffer::Instance& data, bool end_stream)\n```\n- Response body data is encoded and sent downstream\n\n**Phase 3: Response Trailers**\n```cpp\nvoid ActiveStream::encodeTrailers(ResponseTrailerMap& trailers)\n```\n- Trailers complete the response\n\n### Stream-Level Concerns\n\n**Timeouts**:\n- **Request timeout**: How long to wait for request to arrive from downstream\n- **Duration timeout**: Maximum time from request headers to response headers\n- **Idle timeout**: Inactivity timeout\n\n**Tracing**: Each stream has a `Tracing::Span` that can be started by the tracer\n\n**Access logging**: Combined from both connection-level and filter-level access log handlers\n\n**Source files**:\n- `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.h` (lines 141-450)\n- `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc` (stream processing methods)\n\n---\n\n## 3. FilterManager and the HTTP Filter Chain\n\n### Responsibilities\n\n`FilterManager` (source/common/http/filter_manager.h/.cc) is the per-stream filter chain execution engine. It:\n\n1. Creates filter instances via `FilterChainFactory`\n2. Manages decoder and encoder filter chains\n3. Iterates through filters in the correct order\n4. Handles filter return statuses (Continue, StopIteration, SendLocalReply, etc.)\n5. Buffers data when filters stop iteration\n6. Manages per-filter state and watermarks\n\n### Filter Chain Structure\n\nFilters are organized in two chains:\n\n```cpp\nstruct StreamDecoderFilters {\n  std::vector<ActiveStreamDecoderFilterPtr> entries_;\n  // Iterates forward: filter[0], filter[1], ..., filter[N]\n};\n\nstruct StreamEncoderFilters {\n  std::vector<ActiveStreamEncoderFilterPtr> entries_;\n  // Iterates reverse: filter[N], ..., filter[1], filter[0]\n};\n```\n\n**Why reverse iteration for encoders?**\n\nIf filters are configured as: `[A, B, C]`\n- **Decoder**: A \u2192 B \u2192 C (request flows forward)\n- **Encoder**: C \u2192 B \u2192 A (response flows backward, last decoder to respond first)\n\nThis allows filters to see the response in the reverse order they saw the request.\n\n### Request Path: Decoder Filter Chain\n\n```\n[Downstream]\n     \u2193\n[Router reads headers from downstream]\n     \u2193\nActiveStream::decodeHeaders()\n     \u2193\nFilterManager::decodeHeaders()\n     \u2193\nFilter[0]::decodeHeaders()\n     \u2193\nFilter[1]::decodeHeaders()\n     \u2193\nFilter[N]::decodeHeaders() [Router Filter - terminal filter]\n     \u2193\n[Route selected, upstream pool acquired]\n     \u2193\nRouter creates UpstreamRequest\n```\n\nEach filter receives the status from `decodeHeaders()`:\n\n```cpp\nenum class FilterHeadersStatus {\n  Continue,              // Continue to next filter\n  StopIteration,         // Stop but don't buffer\n  StopAllIteration,      // Stop and buffer subsequent frames\n  ContinueAndEndStream,  // Continue but signal end\n  // ...\n};\n```\n\n- If a filter returns `StopAllIteration`, the FilterManager buffers any subsequent data/trailers\n- When the filter calls `continueDecoding()`, iteration resumes from that filter\n\n**Data frame processing**:\n\n```cpp\nFilterManager::decodeData(Buffer::Instance& data, bool end_stream)\n```\n\nData flows through the same filter chain. Filters can:\n- Modify the buffer in-place\n- Replace the entire buffer\n- Buffer data internally and consume it\n- Pass data through unchanged\n\n**Trailers**:\n\n```cpp\nFilterManager::decodeTrailers(RequestTrailerMapPtr&& trailers)\n```\n\nTrailers complete the request body and flow through decoders in the same order.\n\n### Response Path: Encoder Filter Chain\n\nWhen response arrives from upstream:\n\n```\n[Upstream Response arrives]\n     \u2193\nUpstreamRequest::decodeHeaders() [receives upstream 200 OK]\n     \u2193\nRouter Filter internal processing\n     \u2193\nRouter invokes FilterManager::encodeHeaders() [backward through filter chain]\n     \u2193\nFilter[N-1]::encodeHeaders()\n     \u2193\nFilter[1]::encodeHeaders()\n     \u2193\nFilter[0]::encodeHeaders()\n     \u2193\nActiveStream::encodeHeaders() [sends to codec]\n     \u2193\n[Codec encodes and sends downstream]\n```\n\nEncoder filters work similarly to decoder filters but in reverse order.\n\n### Filter Callbacks and State Management\n\nFilters can access stream information and control flow:\n\n```cpp\n// From StreamFilterCallbacks interface\nclass StreamFilterCallbacks {\npublic:\n  OptRef<const Network::Connection> connection();\n  Router::RouteConstSharedPtr route();\n  void resetStream(Http::StreamResetReason reason,\n                   absl::string_view transport_failure_reason);\n  Upstream::ClusterInfoConstSharedPtr clusterInfo();\n  StreamInfo::StreamInfo& streamInfo();\n\n  // Access headers\n  RequestHeaderMapOptRef requestHeaders();\n  ResponseHeaderMapOptRef responseHeaders();\n};\n```\n\n### Watermark Buffering\n\nWhen a filter calls `setBufferLimit()`, FilterManager enforces memory limits:\n\n```cpp\nvoid setBufferLimit(uint64_t limit);\n```\n\nIf buffered data exceeds this limit:\n- Watermark callback triggers\n- Upstream reading is disabled\n- Data stops flowing until buffer drains\n\n### Local Replies\n\nA filter can generate a local reply without contacting upstream:\n\n```cpp\nvoid FilterManager::sendLocalReply(\n    Code code,\n    absl::string_view body,\n    const std::function<void(ResponseHeaderMap& headers)>& modify_headers,\n    const absl::optional<Grpc::Status::GrpcStatus> grpc_status,\n    absl::string_view details)\n```\n\nThis causes:\n- All decoder filters to be skipped for this stream\n- Response headers/body to be created locally\n- Response to flow through encoder filters\n- Stream to complete without upstream contact\n\n### Match-Based Filter Configuration\n\nFilterManager supports dynamic filter configuration via matchers. Filters can have:\n- **Route-specific config**: Set by router based on matched route\n- **Match tree config**: Set based on request/response matching\n\n**Source files**:\n- Header: `source/common/http/filter_manager.h` (lines 34-250)\n- Implementation: `source/common/http/filter_manager.cc` (filter chain iteration)\n- FilterChainFactory: `source/common/http/conn_manager_config.h` (calls `createFilterChain()`)\n\n---\n\n## 4. Router Filter: Route Selection and Upstream Dispatch\n\n### Responsibilities\n\nThe Router Filter (source/common/router/router.h/.cc) is the terminal decoder filter that:\n\n1. Selects a route from `RouteConfiguration`\n2. Obtains a load balanced upstream host\n3. Gets (or creates) an HTTP connection pool for that host\n4. Creates an `UpstreamRequest` to forward the request\n5. Handles retries, timeouts, and request hedging\n6. Processes upstream response and sends it back through encoder filters\n\n### Route Selection\n\n**Route Selection Process**:\n\n```cpp\nHttp::FilterHeadersStatus Filter::decodeHeaders(\n    Http::RequestHeaderMap& headers, bool end_stream)\n```\n\n1. **Find cluster**: The router uses the decoded headers to find a matching route:\n   ```cpp\n   RouteConstSharedPtr route = decoder_callbacks_->route();\n   ```\n   Route selection uses:\n   - Request path (prefix, exact, or regex match)\n   - Request headers\n   - Virtual host match\n   - Scoped routing configuration (if configured)\n\n2. **Extract route entry**: From the matched route, get the RouteEntry:\n   ```cpp\n   RouteEntryConstSharedPtr route_entry = route->routeEntry();\n   ```\n\n3. **Select cluster**: Each route entry specifies a cluster:\n   ```cpp\n   absl::string_view cluster_name = route_entry->clusterName();\n   ```\n\n4. **Get cluster**: From the ClusterManager:\n   ```cpp\n   Upstream::ThreadLocalCluster* cluster =\n       config_->cm_.getThreadLocalCluster(cluster_name);\n   ```\n\n### Host Selection and Connection Pool\n\nOnce a cluster is selected:\n\n```cpp\n// Get load balancer from the cluster\nauto load_balancer = cluster->loadBalancer();\n\n// Select a host using load balancing algorithm\nUpstream::HostConstSharedPtr host =\n    load_balancer.chooseHost(load_balancer_context);\n```\n\nThe `LoadBalancerContext` includes:\n- Request headers (for header-based routing)\n- Stream info\n- Connection cookies (for session affinity)\n- Hash key (for consistent hashing)\n\nOnce a host is selected:\n\n```cpp\n// Get the HTTP connection pool for this host\nHttp::ConnectionPool::Instance* pool =\n    cluster->httpConnPool(host, route_entry->upstreamOptions());\n```\n\nThe connection pool is responsible for:\n- Creating TCP connections to the upstream host\n- Multiplexing multiple requests over a single connection (H2, H3)\n- Managing connection lifetime and reuse\n- Connection health state\n\n### Upstream Request Creation\n\nOnce a pool is obtained:\n\n```cpp\nupstream_request_ = std::make_unique<UpstreamRequest>(\n    *this,                  // RouterFilterInterface (parent)\n    std::move(conn_pool),   // HTTP connection pool\n    can_send_early_data,\n    can_use_http3,\n    enable_half_close);\n```\n\n### Request Forwarding\n\nThe router forwards request data to the upstream request:\n\n**Headers**:\n```cpp\nFilter::decodeHeaders() \u2192 UpstreamRequest::acceptHeadersFromRouter()\n```\n\n**Body data**:\n```cpp\nFilter::decodeData() \u2192 UpstreamRequest::acceptDataFromRouter()\n```\n\n**Trailers**:\n```cpp\nFilter::decodeTrailers() \u2192 UpstreamRequest::acceptTrailersFromRouter()\n```\n\nThe UpstreamRequest buffers data until an upstream connection is established, then sends it.\n\n### Timeout Management\n\nThe router sets up several timeout timers:\n\n**Request timeout**: Maximum time to wait for complete request\n```cpp\nvoid setupRequestTimeout();\n```\n\n**Response timeout** (per-try): Maximum time to receive response\n```cpp\nvoid setupPerTryTimeout();\n```\n\n**Total timeout**: Maximum time from request start to response complete\n\nIf a timeout fires:\n- Stream is reset\n- Local reply is sent (e.g., 504 Gateway Timeout)\n- Retry logic may kick in (if configured)\n\n### Retry Logic\n\nIf upstream returns an error or times out:\n\n```cpp\nif (shouldRetry(upstream_response, retry_policy)) {\n  retry_attempts_++;\n  resetUpstream();\n  selectUpstreamHost();  // Possibly different host\n  // Retry with new upstream\n}\n```\n\nRetry conditions include:\n- 5xx errors (if retry policy allows)\n- Connection reset\n- Per-try timeout (if retries are available)\n\n### Hedged Requests\n\nIf hedging is enabled:\n\n```cpp\nif (should_hedge) {\n  // Start a new upstream request in parallel with the first one\n  hedged_upstream_requests_.push_back(\n      std::make_unique<UpstreamRequest>(...));\n}\n```\n\nThe first response to arrive wins; others are cancelled.\n\n### Shadow Routing\n\nIf the route specifies a shadow policy:\n\n```cpp\nif (route_entry->shadowPolicy().cluster() != \"\") {\n  // Send a copy of the request to the shadow cluster\n  shadow_request_ = std::make_unique<UpstreamRequest>(...);\n  // Shadow response is logged but not sent downstream\n}\n```\n\n### Response Processing\n\nWhen upstream sends response:\n\n```cpp\nvoid UpstreamRequest::decodeHeaders(\n    Http::ResponseHeaderMapPtr&& headers,\n    bool end_stream)\n```\n\nThe upstream request:\n1. Passes headers to router filter\n2. Router filter invokes encoder filters\n3. Response flows back down through encoder chain\n4. ActiveStream::encodeHeaders() sends to codec\n\n**Source files**:\n- Header: `source/common/router/router.h` (lines 298-450)\n- Implementation: `source/common/router/router.cc` (lines 64+)\n- UpstreamRequest: `source/common/router/upstream_request.h` (lines 67+)\n\n---\n\n## 5. UpstreamRequest: Upstream Connection Lifecycle\n\n### Responsibilities\n\n`UpstreamRequest` (source/common/router/upstream_request.h/.cc) manages the lifecycle of a single upstream HTTP request:\n\n1. Acquires a connection from the pool\n2. Buffers downstream data until connection is ready\n3. Sends request to upstream\n4. Receives and processes upstream response\n5. Handles per-try timeouts and retries\n6. Manages flow control between downstream and upstream\n\n### Connection Pool Interface\n\nThe UpstreamRequest calls the HTTP connection pool:\n\n```cpp\nclass Http::ConnectionPool::Instance {\npublic:\n  // Request a new stream from the pool\n  Cancellable* newStream(\n      Http::ResponseDecoder& response_decoder,\n      Http::ConnectionPool::Callbacks& callbacks,\n      const StreamOptions& options);\n};\n```\n\nThe pool returns a `Cancellable` that can be used to cancel the request if needed.\n\n### Pool Callbacks\n\nWhen the pool acquires a connection:\n\n```cpp\nvoid UpstreamRequest::onPoolReady(\n    std::unique_ptr<GenericUpstream>&& upstream,\n    Upstream::HostDescriptionConstSharedPtr host,\n    const Network::ConnectionInfoProvider& address_provider,\n    StreamInfo::StreamInfo& info,\n    absl::optional<Http::Protocol> protocol)\n```\n\nThe pool provides:\n- A `GenericUpstream` object (codec wrapper for the upstream connection)\n- The selected host information\n- The actual protocol negotiated (H2, H3, etc.)\n\n### Data Buffering\n\nRequest data is buffered while waiting for upstream connection:\n\n```cpp\nvoid UpstreamRequest::acceptDataFromRouter(Buffer::Instance& data, bool end_stream)\n```\n\nIf the upstream connection isn't ready:\n- Data is buffered in `upstream_buffer_`\n- Backpressure is applied to the router filter via watermarks\n\nOnce connection is ready:\n- Buffered data is flushed to upstream\n- New data flows directly through\n\n### Per-Try Timeout\n\nEach upstream attempt has its own timeout:\n\n```cpp\nvoid UpstreamRequest::setupPerTryTimeout()\n```\n\nIf the upstream doesn't respond within this timeout:\n- Upstream connection is reset\n- Retry logic is triggered (if allowed)\n- Or local 504 reply is sent\n\n### Per-Try Codec Filter Chain\n\nThe upstream request can have its own HTTP filter chain for transforming upstream request/response:\n\n```cpp\nstd::unique_ptr<UpstreamFilterManager> upstream_filter_manager_;\n```\n\nThese filters allow transforming the request before sending upstream (e.g., adding headers) or transforming the response before sending downstream.\n\n### Watermark Management\n\nUpstreamRequest manages flow control:\n\n```cpp\nstruct DownstreamWatermarkManager : Http::DownstreamWatermarkCallbacks {\n  // Called when response buffer exceeds high watermark\n  void onAboveWriteBufferHighWatermark();\n\n  // Called when response buffer drops below low watermark\n  void onBelowWriteBufferLowWatermark();\n};\n```\n\nThis pauses/resumes downstream reading when upstream response buffer fills up.\n\n### Reset and Cleanup\n\nIf the upstream connection fails or is reset:\n\n```cpp\nvoid UpstreamRequest::onResetStream(\n    Http::StreamResetReason reason,\n    absl::string_view transport_failure_reason)\n```\n\nThe router filter can decide to:\n- Retry with a different host\n- Send a local reply (e.g., 503 Service Unavailable)\n- Reset the downstream stream\n\n**Source files**:\n- Header: `source/common/router/upstream_request.h` (lines 67-250)\n- Implementation: `source/common/router/upstream_request.cc`\n\n---\n\n## 6. Cluster Manager and Upstream Connectivity\n\n### Responsibilities\n\n`ClusterManagerImpl` (source/common/upstream/cluster_manager_impl.h/.cc) provides:\n\n1. **Cluster management**: Creates and manages cluster objects from configuration\n2. **Connection pooling**: Provides per-host HTTP connection pools\n3. **Load balancing**: Returns hosts to connect to\n4. **Health checking**: Tracks endpoint health\n5. **Outlier detection**: Removes unhealthy hosts\n\n### Cluster Abstraction\n\nA cluster represents a logical group of upstream endpoints:\n\n```cpp\nclass Cluster {\npublic:\n  // Load balancing\n  LoadBalancer& loadBalancer();\n\n  // Connection pool\n  Http::ConnectionPool::Instance* httpConnPool(\n      Upstream::HostConstSharedPtr host,\n      const Http::HttpConnectionPoolOptions& options);\n\n  // Health/monitoring\n  Health::HealthChecker* healthChecker();\n  Outlier::OutlierDetector* outlierDetector();\n};\n```\n\n### Load Balancer Selection\n\nThe cluster has a load balancer that selects hosts:\n\n```cpp\nclass LoadBalancer {\npublic:\n  // Select a host based on context\n  ChooseHostStatus chooseHost(LoadBalancerContext* context);\n};\n```\n\nDifferent load balancing algorithms:\n- **Round Robin**: Cycles through all healthy hosts\n- **Least Request**: Selects host with fewest active requests\n- **Ring Hash**: Consistent hashing for session affinity\n- **Random**: Random selection\n- **Maglev**: Another consistent hashing algorithm\n\nThe context provides:\n- Request headers\n- Hash key (if using hash-based LB)\n- Priority (for multi-priority routing)\n- Cookies (for session affinity)\n\n### Connection Pool Structure\n\nEach host has a connection pool:\n\n```cpp\nclass HttpConnPoolImplBase : public Http::ConnectionPool::Instance {\npublic:\n  // Request a new stream\n  Cancellable* newStream(ResponseDecoder& decoder, Callbacks& callbacks);\n\n  // Connection management\n  void drainConnections();\n  bool hasActiveConnections();\n};\n```\n\n**For HTTP/1.1**:\n- One physical TCP connection per stream (multiplexing not supported)\n- Pool maintains a queue of pending requests\n- When a connection completes, next pending request uses it\n\n**For HTTP/2**:\n- Multiple streams share a single TCP connection\n- Pool creates up to `max_connections` physical connections\n- Streams are multiplexed across these connections\n- Each connection can handle many concurrent streams\n\n**For HTTP/3/QUIC**:\n- Similar to HTTP/2 but over UDP/QUIC\n- Better connection establishment latency\n\n### Active Client (Physical Connection)\n\nEach physical connection is managed by an `ActiveClient`:\n\n```cpp\nclass ActiveClient : public GenericUpstream {\npublic:\n  // Send headers/data/trailers to upstream\n  void sendHeaders(RequestHeaderMap& headers, bool end_stream);\n  void sendData(Buffer::Instance& data, bool end_stream);\n\n  // Codec for encoding/decoding\n  CodecClient& codec();\n};\n```\n\nThe pool manages:\n- Creating new ActiveClients when needed\n- Reusing idle ActiveClients for new requests\n- Removing unhealthy ActiveClients\n- Enforcing connection limits\n\n### Health Checking\n\nIf health checking is configured for a cluster:\n\n```cpp\nHealth::HealthChecker* health_checker = cluster->healthChecker();\n```\n\nHealth checkers periodically probe endpoints (via HTTP or other protocol) and mark hosts as healthy/unhealthy. The load balancer only sends traffic to healthy hosts.\n\n### Outlier Detection\n\nIf outlier detection is enabled:\n\n```cpp\nOutlier::OutlierDetector* detector = cluster->outlierDetector();\n```\n\nThe detector tracks:\n- Request latencies\n- Error rates\n- Consecutive errors\n\nIf a host exceeds thresholds, it's temporarily removed from load balancing (ejected). After a recovery timeout, it's re-enabled.\n\n### Priority and Locality-Based Routing\n\nClusters support multi-tier load balancing:\n\n```cpp\nenum class Priority {\n  Primary = 0,    // Try primary endpoints first\n  Secondary = 1,  // Fall back to secondary if primary exhausted\n};\n```\n\nEach priority level has endpoints in different localities. The load balancer:\n- Tries primary priority first\n- Falls back to secondary if all primary unhealthy\n- Within a priority, may prefer endpoints in the local zone\n\n**Source files**:\n- Header: `source/common/upstream/cluster_manager_impl.h` (lines 52-250)\n- Implementation: `source/common/upstream/cluster_manager_impl.cc`\n- Cluster abstraction: `source/common/upstream/upstream_impl.h`\n\n---\n\n## Data Flow: Request Arrival to Upstream Dispatch\n\n### Complete Request Path\n\n```\n\u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510\n\u2502 DOWNSTREAM CONNECTION ESTABLISHED                             \u2502\n\u2514\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2518\n                           \u2193\n\u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510\n\u2502 ConnectionManagerImpl::onNewConnection()                       \u2502\n\u2502 - Extension Points\n\n### 1. HTTP Filters\n\nUsers extend Envoy by implementing HTTP filters:\n\n```cpp\nclass StreamDecoderFilter {\npublic:\n  virtual FilterHeadersStatus decodeHeaders(\n      RequestHeaderMap& headers, bool end_stream);\n  virtual FilterDataStatus decodeData(\n      Buffer::Instance& data, bool end_stream);\n  virtual FilterTrailersStatus decodeTrailers(\n      RequestTrailerMap& trailers);\n  virtual void setDecoderFilterCallbacks(StreamDecoderFilterCallbacks&);\n};\n\nclass StreamEncoderFilter {\npublic:\n  virtual Filter1xxHeadersStatus encode1xxHeaders(ResponseHeaderMap&);\n  virtual FilterHeadersStatus encodeHeaders(\n      ResponseHeaderMap& headers, bool end_stream);\n  virtual FilterDataStatus encodeData(\n      Buffer::Instance& data, bool end_stream);\n  virtual FilterTrailersStatus encodeTrailers(\n      ResponseTrailerMap& trailers);\n  virtual void setEncoderFilterCallbacks(StreamEncoderFilterCallbacks&);\n};\n```\n\n**Extension points for filters**:\n- Inspect/modify request headers (e.g., add trace headers)\n- Inspect/buffer request data (e.g., for WAF)\n- Generate local replies (e.g., authentication)\n- Inspect/modify response headers (e.g., add CORS headers)\n- Access route/cluster info via callbacks\n- Implement custom routing logic via match trees\n\n**Built-in filters** (in order):\n- Microversion filter\n- Router filter (terminal decoder filter)\n- Access log filter\n\n### 2. Route Selection\n\nRoutes are configured via `RouteConfiguration` and can be:\n\n```cpp\nclass RouteEntry {\npublic:\n  // Matching criteria\n  virtual bool pathMatchCriterion(...);\n  virtual absl::optional<StringMatcher> hostPattern();\n\n  // Route actions\n  virtual absl::string_view clusterName();\n  virtual TimeoutData timeout();\n  virtual const RetryPolicy& retryPolicy();\n  virtual bool shadowPolicy();\n};\n```\n\nUsers can:\n- Define static routes in bootstrap config\n- Use RDS (Route Discovery Service) for dynamic routing\n- Use weighted clusters for canary deployments\n- Use retry policies and request hedging\n- Use shadow routing for testing\n\n### 3. Load Balancing\n\nUsers can implement custom load balancers:\n\n```cpp\nclass LoadBalancer {\npublic:\n  virtual ChooseHostStatus chooseHost(LoadBalancerContext* context);\n};\n```\n\nCustom load balancers can:\n- Access request headers from context\n- Use hash keys for consistent hashing\n- Implement custom affinity logic\n- Apply custom weighting schemes\n\n**Built-in LBs**:\n- Round Robin\n- Least Request\n- Ring Hash\n- Maglev Hash\n- Random\n- Weighted Cluster\n\n### 4. Cluster Extensions\n\nClusters support custom implementations:\n\n```cpp\nclass Cluster {\npublic:\n  virtual LoadBalancer& loadBalancer();\n  virtual Http::ConnectionPool::Instance* httpConnPool(...);\n  virtual HealthChecker* healthChecker();\n  virtual OutlierDetector* outlierDetector();\n};\n```\n\nUsers can implement:\n- Custom health checkers (beyond HTTP probes)\n- Custom connection pool implementations\n- Custom outlier detection algorithms\n- Custom load balancer factories\n\n### 5. Access Logging\n\nAccess logs are configured per stream and can use various sinks and formats:\n\n```cpp\nclass AccessLog {\npublic:\n  virtual void log(const RequestHeaderMap* request_headers,\n                   const ResponseHeaderMap* response_headers,\n                   const ResponseTrailerMap* response_trailers,\n                   const StreamInfo& stream_info);\n};\n```\n\nUsers can:\n- Log to file, syslog, or custom sink\n- Use built-in formatters or custom formatters\n- Apply sampling or conditional logging\n- Access detailed stream info (timings, response codes, etc.)\n\n### 6. Tracing\n\nIf tracing is configured, each stream has a `Tracing::Span`:\n\n```cpp\nclass Tracer {\npublic:\n  virtual SpanPtr startSpan(const Config& config, ...);\n};\n```\n\nSpans are created at:\n- Request ingress (if configured)\n- Per operation (if router specifies operation name)\n- Per upstream request (if enabled)\n\nUsers can integrate with:\n- Jaeger\n- Zipkin\n- Datadog\n- Custom tracers\n\n---\n\n## Error Handling\n\n### Downstream Errors\n\n**Codec errors**: If the codec fails to parse HTTP (invalid headers, etc.):\n- Connection is closed\n- Partial streams are reset\n- `http_connection_errors` counter incremented\n\n**Filter errors**: If a filter returns an error or calls `resetStream()`:\n- All downstream and upstream resources are cleaned up\n- Connection may remain open for other streams\n- Access log is generated\n\n**Local replies**: If a filter generates a local reply (no upstream):\n- Reply flows through remaining encoder filters\n- Codec encodes response\n- Connection remains open\n\n### Upstream Errors\n\n**Pool failures**: If the HTTP connection pool can't acquire a connection:\n- Router filter invokes retry logic (if configured)\n- Or sends local 503 Service Unavailable\n- Stream completes with error flags in stream info\n\n**Upstream reset**: If upstream closes the connection:\n- UpstreamRequest detects reset\n- Router filter decides whether to retry\n- Or forwards reset to downstream (triggers downstream reset)\n\n**Per-try timeout**: If per-try timeout fires:\n- UpstreamRequest is reset\n- Router retries (if allowed)\n- Or sends local 504 Gateway Timeout\n\n**Upstream 5xx**: If upstream returns 5xx error:\n- Router checks retry policy\n- If retryable and retries available, retries with different host\n- Or forwards 5xx to downstream\n\n### Resource Limits\n\n**Overload handling**: During overload:\n- `HcmDecodeHeaders` shed point can reject new streams\n- `HcmCodecCreation` shed point can prevent codec instantiation\n- `StopAcceptingRequests` can reject all new requests\n- `DisableHttpKeepAlive` forces connection closure after each request\n\n**Watermark backpressure**: When buffers fill:\n- Upstream reading is paused\n- Downstream is paused via connection watermarks\n- Flow resumes when buffers drain\n\n---\n\n## Summary\n\nThe HTTP Connection Manager implements a clean, composable architecture:\n\n1. **ConnectionManagerImpl** owns the downstream connection and creates streams\n2. **ActiveStream** wraps each request/response and owns the filter chain\n3. **FilterManager** executes the filter chain in both directions\n4. **Router Filter** is the terminal decoder that selects upstream and creates UpstreamRequest\n5. **UpstreamRequest** manages the upstream connection and bridges upstream response back\n6. **ClusterManager** provides connection pools and host selection\n\nThis design allows:\n- **Extensibility**: Custom filters can inspect/modify requests and responses\n- **Composability**: Filters are independent and can be mixed and matched\n- **Efficiency**: Multiplexed connections (H2/H3) and lazy initialization reduce overhead\n- **Observability**: Detailed stream info, tracing, and access logs at each stage\n- **Resilience**: Retries, timeouts, health checking, and outlier detection\n\nThe architecture clearly separates concerns: network/codec handling, filter chain execution, routing/load balancing, and connection pooling. Each component has well-defined responsibilities and interfaces, making it straightforward to understand and extend Envoy's HTTP processing.\n",

1. WRITE /workspace/documentation.md
# Envoy HTTP Connection Manager Architecture

## Overview

The HTTP Connection Manager (HCM) is the central network filter in Envoy that processes HTTP traffic on a downstream connection. This document explains how the major components interact to receive HTTP requests on a downstream connection, process them through a filter chain, and dispatch them to upstream clusters.

The HCM architecture follows a clear separation of concerns:
- **ConnectionManagerImpl**: Owns the downstream connection lifecycle and manages individual streams
- **ActiveStream**: Wraps a single HTTP request/response pair and owns the filter chain
- **FilterManager**: Executes the per-stream filter chain in both directions (decode and encode)
- **Router Filter**: Terminal decoder filter that selects an upstream cluster and route
- **UpstreamRequest & Cluster Manager**: Handle upstream connection pooling and host selection

## 1. ConnectionManagerImpl: Connection Lifecycle and Stream Management

### Responsibilities

`ConnectionManagerImpl` (source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.h/.cc) is the entry point for HTTP processing. It implements three key interfaces:

1. **Network::ReadFilter** — Receives raw bytes from the network layer
2. **ServerConnectionCallbacks** — Receives decoded HTTP streams from the codec
3. **Network::ConnectionCallbacks** — Handles connection lifecycle events (reset, close)

### Key Features

#### 1.1 Network Ingress: onData()

When data arrives on a downstream connection:

```cpp
Network::FilterStatus ConnectionManagerImpl::onData(Buffer::Instance& data, bool end_stream)
```

- **Lazy codec instantiation**: The codec is created on first `onData()` call (or on `onConnection()` for H3/QUIC)
  - HTTP/1.1 uses `Http1::CodecImpl`
  - HTTP/2 uses `Http2::CodecImpl`
  - HTTP/3 uses `Q
